Chapter 1

Br i d ger Insight XG
LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG (XG) is a risk management product that lets you use search services
to compare your input entities against public and proprietary data. This functionality helps you lower
compliance costs and protect yourself from regulatory risk.
As part of the search, you tell XG which settings to use, who to assign the alerts to, and whether to store
the results in the XG database.
You also use XG to complete case management and workflow actions on the alerts and to manage batch
runs. A batch run contains the details about a batch search or an alert import and any associated alerts.
You can query, view, update, and delete alerts that are stored in the XG database. For example, you can
change the alert assignment or add an alert to an accept list.
In addition, you use XG to manage accept lists and custom screening lists. Accept lists can help you
suppress list screening matches in new searches that you have already processed and determined to be
false positives or determined that updates to the entity records need to be monitored. Custom screening
lists can help you flag entities in list screening searches that are unique to your organization.

Searchable Data
XG lets you search either structured input data or unstructured input data.
Structured data is organized into defined fields that lets XG treat like information the same for more
relevant results. You can use custom formats to search business entity records, individual entity records,
or unknown entity records. You can also use the following corresponding default formats to search
payment transaction data:
ACH (Automated Clearing House) files
For information about ACH record content and format, see https://www.nacha.org. For information
about supported ACH formats and the data that is processed by XG, see the related article that
is available on the LexisNexis® Risk Solutions Customer Support Hub at https://lnrs.my.site.com/
CustomerSupportHub/s/article/2093.
Fedwire files
For information about Fedwire record content and format, see https://www.frbservices.org. For
information about Fedwire file processing in XG, see the related article that is available on the
Customer Support Hub at https://lnrs.my.site.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/2148.

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 9

CONFIDENTIAL

ISO (International Organization for Standardization) 20022 files
For information about ISO 20022 record content and format, see https://www.iso20022.org. For
information about ISO 20022 file processing in XG, see the related article that is available on the
Customer Support Hub at https://lnrs.my.site.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/2064.
SWIFT (Society for Worldwide Interbank Financial Telecommunication) files
For information about SWIFT record content and format, see https://www.swift.com. For
information about SWIFT file processing in XG, see the related article on the Customer Support
Hub at https://lnrs.my.site.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/1883 or https://lnrs.my.site.com/
CustomerSupportHub/s/article/2635.
For information about supported ACH formats and the data processed by XG, see the appropriate
payment screening technical reference guide that is available on the Customer Support Hub.
Unstructured data is not organized into defined fields. You can search unstructured data as a text record
or by using the Unstructured format. A text record contains one required field of unstructured text and
optional ID fields. When you search unstructured data, XG must search files one text string at a time. This
type of search may yield different results than when XG searches a file with identified fields.

SOAP API
The SOAP API for XG lets you incorporate the XG functionality into your existing systems. This
functionality lets you manage web service access, searching, results, and lists. Each request contains
a SOAP (Simple Object Access Protocol) message with a method that defines an action to be performed.
XG also offers a REST API. For more information, see the related documentation that is available on the
Customer Support Hub at https://lnrs.my.site.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/2016.
The SOAP API includes the following interfaces:
Account Interface
You use the Account interface to access the web service and to manage passwords.
Search Interface
You use the Search interface to perform searches. You can specify a predefined search that was
created in the XG application, or you can configure a unique search in the request. You can search
screening lists that are provided by LexisNexis® Risk Solutions to help your organization conduct
due diligence and comply with global mandates and government regulations. You can view the lists
that are available for searching. You can search LexisNexis® FraudPoint® Score to help predict the
likelihood that applicant input information is of unreliable authenticity, fraudulent, or materially
misrepresented. You can search with LexisNexis® InstantID® to help you verify an identity or alert you
to indicators of potential risk.

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 10

CONFIDENTIAL

Results Interface
You use the Results interface to manage your alerts. You can query, view, and delete a batch run. You
can add, view, and delete files that are attached to alerts.
ListMaintenance Interface
You use the ListMaintenance interface to manage accept lists and custom screening lists. You can
add, query, view, update, and delete a list or records in a list. You can index a custom screening list.
The SOAP API accepts XML messages over SOAP. The WSDL (Web Services Description Language) defines
the SOAP interfaces and allows tools to create proxy objects to generate and invoke the appropriate
SOAP methods. These SOAP methods are then sent over TCP or HTTPS. For each request, a method
defines an action that is performed either by or upon an instance of a class. The response also returns
information in classes.
The WSDL has been tested with Microsoft Visual Studio and SoapUI. For Python, spaces in web
addresses need to be escaped. Other programs may also be able to consume the WSDL.
The WSDL is often used in combination with SOAP and XML Schema to provide web services over
the internet. A client program that connects to a web service can read the WSDL to determine what
functions are available on the server. Any special data types used are embedded in the WSDL file in the
form of XML Schema. The client can then use SOAP to actually call one of the functions listed in the
WSDL. If your staff has limited SOAP knowledge, then you can use a third-party tool to create client
proxy objects from the WSDL.
The way that you access the SOAP API depends on your product and environment:
XG Service
Depending on your account, you access the WSDL at:
https://<Your XG Environment>/LN.WebServices/<web service version>/XGServices.svc?
wsdl.

XG Enterprise
The WSDL location is configured when you install the product. See the LexisNexis® Bridger Insight®
XG Enterprise Installation technical reference guide.
The environment is displayed in the browser address bar for the XG user interface.

system could become unusable.

Chapter 2

W e b Ser vi ce Setup
LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG (XG) web services provide setup flexibility. Before you implement the
services, consider your environment and business requirements.

Communication Protocols and Programming Languages
XG web services support HTTP/HTTPS as the communication protocol. The HTTP/HTTPS web service
is hosted in IIS (Internet Information Services) and exposes both a WCF (Windows Communication
Foundation) MEX (metadata exchange) endpoint and an HTTP GET method.
You can use any programming language that can consume a WCF MEX endpoint or a WSDL (Web
Services Description Language).

Communication Architecture
You can add additional application servers and IIS servers to help ensure that if one server fails, one or
more servers are still available to handle client requests.
However, if multiple servers are used, then a load balancer is required to distribute client requests
between servers. IIS communicates with one or more application servers through the TCP/IP interface.
Depending upon load, adding additional application servers and IIS servers into the system may increase
performance. However, if multiple servers are used, then a load balancer is required to distribute client
requests between servers. Load balancing may be done through hardware, software, or internal load
balancing.

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 15

CONFIDENTIAL

Proxy Objects
If you use a programming language that can consume a WCF MEX endpoint, then
client proxies can be auto-generated or can be created through ChannelFactory<IAccount>,
ChannelFactory<IListMaintenance>, ChannelFactory<IResults>, or ChannelFactory<ISearch>.
Examples of auto-generated proxies are those generated by svcutil.exe (or a similar tool) or those
generated when a service reference or web reference is added to a project in Visual Studio.
For best performance when auto-generated proxies are used, reuse the proxy object. Be sure to develop
code to handle instances when the proxy object channel is in a faulted state.
It may not always be possible to reuse the proxy object. For example, while the proxy object is
thread safe there can be contention issues if you use it in multiple threads. It is possible to get good
performance if you take advantage of the proxy object constructors that do not take Binding as an
argument and if you do not use the ChannelFactory, Endpoint, and ClientCredentials elements. This
allows for the underlying code to internally cache the ChannelFactory object, which makes for efficient
creation of proxy objects. If this is not possible, then consider using proxy pooling.
For best performance when ChannelFactory<IAccount>, ChannelFactory<IListMaintenance>,
ChannelFactory<IResults>, or ChannelFactory<ISearch> is used, create a single instance of the channel
factory and then use its CreateChannel method to create client proxy objects.
If you use a programming language that can consume a WCF MEX endpoint, then
client proxy objects (either auto-generated or created through ChannelFactory<IAccount>,
ChannelFactory<IListMaintenance>, ChannelFactory<IResults>, or ChannelFactory<ISearch>) are thread
safe. However, there can be some contention issues when the same object is used in multiple threads.

Security
XG Enterprise clients can configure the security tag for web service bindings. This setting is not available
to XG Service clients.
This configuration is typically completed when XG Enterprise is installed. The equivalent settings must
also be set in the application and IIS.
For the mode attribute in the security tag, you may specify one of the following values:
None
Messages are not secured in any way. It is the fastest option, but only use it if messages do not need
to be securely transmitted between the client and the server.

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 16

CONFIDENTIAL

Message
Messages are secured at the message level using WS-Security and other specification. It is transportprotocol independent, more extensible, and ensures end-to-end security. However, it is several times
slower than transport security.
Transport
Messages are secured at the transport level using, for example, HTTPS. This option is widely adopted
and less complex. However, it provides only point-to-point security.
TransportWithMessageCredential
Messages are secured using message security to authenticate the client and transport security to
authenticate the server and provide message security. This option is only slightly slower than the
transport mode. However, like transport mode, it provides only point-to-point security.
End-to-end security means that the message is secure even when routed through intermediary
application nodes. Point-to-point security means that the message is secure only from one application
node to the next application node so intermediary application nodes have access to the message.
With the basicHttpBinding binding used in the web.config file, if you use the HTTP protocol, then you
must use the mode None. If you use the HTTPS protocol, then you must use the mode Transport. The
installer sets these appropriately. The web.config file is located in the XG installation folder.
With the netTcpBinding binding used in the BridgerInsightService.exe.config file, by default the
mode is set to None. The BridgerInsightService.exe.config file is located in the XG installation
folder. If the security mode is Transport, then the security tag must contain a transport tag (Message by
default) and the clientCredentialType value needs to be one of the following:
None
The WCF service does not authenticate the client.
Windows
Clients are authenticated against Active Directory using a Windows token. The service is
authenticated by the Windows credentials or by the SSL (secure sockets layer) certificate if using
HTTPS.
There are other possible client credential types, but they have not been tested with XG web
services.

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 17

CONFIDENTIAL

Rate Limits
XG web services supports rate limitations for improved system stability and scalability. Rate limits also
help protect against slow performance and denial-of-service attacks for systems that are accessible
outside of an organization's firewall.
XG Enterprise clients can use the following value to enable this feature in the installation configuration
files: <globalSymbol name="EnableApiRateLimit">false</globalSymbol>. The feature must also be
configured for each client instance in Enterprise Manager.
The following response headers are returned when rate limiting is enabled.
X-RateLimit-Limit
The header value is an integer that shows how many requests are allowed per period.
X-RateLimit-Remaining
The header value is an integer that shows how many requests can be submitted in the current period
before rate limiting is enforced and requests will start to fail.
X-RateLimit-Reset
The header value is an integer that shows how many seconds until the period expires and a new
timer begins. If you have reached your rate limit, then you cannot submit requests until the period
expires and a new timer begins.
When the rate limit is surpassed, the web service response returns the following error: The number of

requests received has exceeded the configured rate limit of # per (second|minute|hour).

Bridger Insight XG Access
XG web services requires users to provide certain credentials for access.
You must provide the following credentials:
Client ID
The client ID is required for most product setups. The client ID identifies the XG client instance of the
user who sent the request.
User ID
The user ID is required if your system does not use Windows authentication.
Password
The XG user password is required if your system does not use Windows authentication.

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 18

CONFIDENTIAL

In the Account interface, you can use the GetDaysUntilPasswordExpires method to determine when
the password expires. You can use the ChangePassword method to change the password.
XG passwords, along with their associated user accounts, can also be managed in the XG user
interface. For more information, see the LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG Help.
DPPA (Driver’s Privacy Protection Act) permissible use
A DPPA permissible use is required for LexisNexis® FraudPoint® Score searches and LexisNexis®
InstantID® searches on individual entities.
GLBA (Gramm‐Leach‐Bliley Act) permissible use
A GLBA permissible use is required for FraudPoint Score searches and InstantID searches.
The user that sends the request must have the division access and the role access that is required to
perform the actions. For more information, see the LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG Help.

Web Service Planning
You should consider a number of factors to best implement XG web services.

A c c o un t Int erface
LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG (XG) web services provides an Account interface that you can use to
manage XG passwords.
User accounts, passwords, the password length, and the password expiration period are managed in the
XG interface. For more information, see the LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG Help.
The Account interface lets you complete the following tasks:
• Change the password that is associated with an XG user account.
• Get the number of days until a password expires.
Related Information
C# Code Examples on page 211

ChangePassword Method
The ChangePassword method changes the XG password that is associated with the user ID.
Syntax
bool ChangePassword(ClientContext context, string newPassword)

Parameters
The method contains the following parameters:
context
The ClientContext class contains the XG client information and the XG session information.
newPassword
The parameter contains the new XG password.
Passwords are case sensitive.
Passwords should be secure and confidential.

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 20

CONFIDENTIAL

The password must meet the following requirements:
• The password must contain at least one letter, number, and special character. Examples of
special characters include !, @, or #.
• The password cannot contain the user ID or its reverse.
• The password cannot be one of the previous 12 passwords.
Return Values
If the method succeeds, then the response returns True.
If the method fails or generates an error, then the response returns an Error class.

Chapter 4

S e ar c h In t erface
LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG (XG) web services provide a Search interface that you can use to perform
searches on your input information.
You can choose to write search results to your XG database for further processing. You can access these
alerts through the Results interface or through the XG application.
The Search interface lets you view information about available accept lists and screening lists. You
can perform list screening searches on accept lists, custom screening lists, and screening lists that are
provided by LexisNexis® Risk Solutions. You can also include the LexisNexis® FraudPoint® Score service
and LexisNexis® InstantID® in your searches.
You can configure the settings that XG uses to search your input information by specifying a predefined
search that was created in the XG application. Or, you can provide search configuration settings in the
request.

to view information on accept lists, custom screening lists, and screening lists that are provided by
LexisNexis Risk Solutions.

W a tc h l i s tA u to mat icFalsePositiveRules Class
The WatchlistAutomaticFalsePositiveRules class contains the standard rules for automatic false positives.
You should not use the standard rules for automatic false positives in combination with rules for
®
LexisNexis Intelligent Match Decision Solution (IMDS).
You can set the standard rules to determine that a list match in an alert is an automatic false positive
when only the input entity name matches a list entity name and the specified data element does not
match. You can also set XG to consider a list match in an alert to be an automatic false positive when the
input name matches a list entity name and the list match meets the White List criteria.

Application of the Rules
You can set multiple rules for automatic false positives. A list match needs to meet only one of the
specified rules for XG to determine that the match is an automatic false positive. However, if any of the
following data elements also matches in the same list match, then the product does not set the match as
an automatic false positive: address, DOB, ID number, or phone number.
An alert can contain multiple list matches. When only some list matches in the alert meet one of the
specified rules, XG generates an alert with an open alert state. By default, this alert contains only the
list matches that do not meet a rule. You can configure the product to also include the list matches that
meet a rule in the alert.
When all list matches in the alert meet one of the selected rules, XG generates an alert with an open
alert state by default. You can configure the product to not generate an alert or to generate an alert with
an Unassigned alert state.
Before alerts with an Unassigned alert state can be set to Closed, the alert state must first be
changed to Open.

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 36

CONFIDENTIAL

Automatic False Positive Example

Your organization decides that matches are false positives when the input entity’s gender and the list
entity’s gender are not the same. You specify the standard rule for gender in the settings that you use to
search your input entity.
You search the following input entity:
Name: Zach Thul
Gender: Female
Address: 503 Waybreeze Blvd

XG finds this list entity match:
Name: Zach Thul
Gender: Male
Address: 111 Waybreeze Blvd

The gender does not match so XG considers the match to be an automatic false positive. However, if the
address had matched, then XG would not consider the match to be an automatic false positive.
If the alert contains only list matches that meet the Automatic False Positive rule for gender, then the
predefined search sets XG to complete one of the following actions:
• The product generates an alert with an open alert state.
• The product generates an alert with an unassigned alert state.
• The product does not generate an alert.
If the alert contains list matches that do not meet the rule, then XG generates an alert with an open alert
state by default. The alert contains the list matches that do not meet the rule. The predefined search
tells the product whether the alert can also contain the list matches that do meet the rule.
These rules are not applied to searches that are processed with the XG - Unstructured format.
You use the XG - Unstructured format to process files with unparsed data that is not provided in
defined fields. Because XG cannot distinguish between addresses, IDs, or other data elements in
unparsed data, XG searches for only names in these files.
Class Elements
Name

Type

Description

Addresses

Boolean

True sets XG to consider a list match in an alert to be

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

an automatic false positive when the following criteria
is met:
• The input name matches a list entity name.
• The following data elements do not match in the
list match: address, DOB, ID number, or phone
number.
• The input address does not match the address of
the list entity.

W a tc h l i s t EFT Mat ch Options Clas s
The WatchlistEFTMatchOptions class contains the ACH (Automated Clearing House) options.
You can set how XG handles IAT (International Automated Clearing House Transaction) records.
The IAT structure includes two U.S. OFAC indicators. These indicators are used to communicate that
an OFAC match was found for one of the entities that is associated with the transaction by screeners
that are external to XG. Typically, XG reports a match if the input IAT record contains either of these
indicators. For records that contain both indicators, XG creates only one alert. XG reports the match

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 43

CONFIDENTIAL

against the originating entity. If the originating entity is not included in the record, then XG reports the
match against the first parsed entity. Along with the match that is reported because of the indicators, XG
also reports any additional matches for entities that are associated with the record.

W a tc h l i s t Fal s eMatc hSettings C lass
The WatchlistFalseMatchSettings class contains the options for false match updates.
XG can be set to generate an alert that contains a false match update when new match information is
found for certain data elements that are in an accept list record.
For a match that was found on a custom screening list, XG can only generate a false match update
if the list is required to contain a unique ID for each record.
False match updates are designed to alert you to new match information that may need further
investigation to determine whether the record should remain on the accept list as a false positive. For
example, if you previously added a match to an accept list that did not contain a matching DOB, and then
XG found a matching DOB in a later search, XG would generate a false match update.

W a tc h l i s t I nt el l ig entMatchDec isi on Solut ion Class
The WatchlistIntelligentMatchDecisionSolution class contains the options for IMDS.
You should not use the standard rules for automatic false positives in combination with rules for
IMDS.
IMDS lets your organization develop rules to automatically process list matches in a way that aligns
with your organization's list screening program and risk profile. The rules leverage input, list, and
match attributes from XG searches to test for evidence of a false positive. IMDS uses specified
rules and a confidence threshold to determine whether a match is an automatic false positive. A
well-planned, tuned, and validated implementation of IMDS can result in increased productivity and
reduced operational costs.

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 47

CONFIDENTIAL

IMDS is available based on your product subscription. Before you can configure IMDS in a
predefined search, the rules must be set up in the system for your XG client instance. For XG
®
®
Enterprise, see LexisNexis Bridger Insight XG Enterprise Manager Help.
If IMDS is configured for your client instance, then you can set the rules and the confidence threshold
that a match must meet to be considered an automatic false positive. The false positive confidence score
indicates how confident the rules are that the match is a false positive. The false positive confidence
score can range from 0.0000 (no confidence that the match is a false positive) to 10.0000 (full confidence
that the match is a false positive).
The false positive confidence score is not the same as the match confidence score (70-100) that XG
provides for each match to indicate how closely the list entity matches the input entity.
For more information about rules for IMDS, see the Rules for LexisNexis® Intelligent Match Decision
Solution technical reference guide.

Application of the Rules
You can set multiple rules for automatic false positives. A list match needs to meet only one of the
specified rules for XG to determine that the match is an automatic false positive. However, if any of the
following data elements also matches in the same list match, then the product does not set the match as
an automatic false positive: address, DOB, ID number, or phone number.
An alert can contain multiple list matches. When only some list matches in the alert meet one of the
specified rules, XG generates an alert with an open alert state. By default, this alert contains only the
list matches that do not meet a rule. You can configure the product to also include the list matches that
meet a rule in the alert.
When all list matches in the alert meet one of the selected rules, XG generates an alert with an open
alert state by default. You can configure the product to not generate an alert or to generate an alert with
an Unassigned alert state.
Class Elements
Name

Type

Description

Confidence

String

This element contains the value for the false positive
confidence score that a match must meet to be
considered an automatic false positive.
Possible values range between 0.0000–10.0000.

RulesName

String

This element contains the rules for IMDS that XG
uses to determine that a match is an automatic false
positive.

Solutions. Matches to this search are not included in alerts and are not stored in the result database.

The InputRecord class contains an input record to be searched. This class is required for all Search

You must provide one of the following elements, which are ordered from highest to lowest priority:
1.
2.
3.
4.

InputEntity
InputText
InputEFT
InputBasicID

If you provide more than one, then XG searches only the element with the highest priority.

Status

String
String

This element contains user-defined information.
This element contains the alert status.

The values are not case sensitive and will reflect the

configured to require an alert status when alerts are
closed or reassigned. If a required alert status is not
set, then an error is returned.

The index indicates the risk that the transaction is
in connection with a real identity that has been
compromised. For example, the identity is applying
with a new address that is not likely associated with
the true owner of the identity. The index range is 1–9.
The index indicates the level of suspicious and highrisk activity that was previously observed for the input
elements. For example, the input elements are tied to
records that were previously deemed to be suspicious
or high risk. The index range is 1–9.
The index indicates the risk that the input identity
is a synthetic identity. For example, this identity
is only reported by credit bureaus or is missing
characteristics of normal identities. The index range
is 1–9.
The index indicates the identity profile is at risk for
being a victim of identity fraud. For example, a highoccupancy location or minors. The index range is 1–9.

DOB Match Levels
The DOB match level indicates the level of the match between the input DOB and the DOB found for the
input entity.
Possible DOB Match Levels
Web Service Value

Description

0

No DOB found or no DOB submitted

1

Nothing matches

2

Only Day matches

3

Only Month matches

4

Only Day and Month match

5

Only Day and Year match

6

Only Year matches

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

CONFIDENTIAL

Web Service Value

Description

7

Only Month and Year match

8

Month, Day, and Year match

WorldCompliance Data Plus Result Classes
The search response may include the classes that contain results for the WorldCompliance Data Plus list.
These results are part of the list screening results and include list entity information.
The WorldCompliance data is organized into multiple segments. For information about WorldCompliance
Data Plus segments, see the Segments for LexisNexis® WorldCompliance™ Data Plus technical reference
guide at https://lnrs.my.site.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/2481.

Chapter 5

R es ul ts I n terfac e
The Results interface lets you manage your alerts. You can also manage alerts through the LexisNexis®
Bridger Insight® XG (XG) application.
For more information, see the LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG Help.

Run Management
The Results interface lets you manage the runs that are stored in the XG database. A run contains the
details about a batch search or an alert import and any associated alerts.
The Results interface lets you perform the following actions on runs:
• View a run.
• Search for a run.
• Delete a run.
Related Information
C# Code Examples on page 211

DeleteRuns Method
The DeleteRuns method deletes the specified runs.
Syntax
List<long> DeleteRuns(ClientContext context, List<long> runIDs)

Parameters
The method contains the following parameters:
context
The ClientContext class contains the XG client information and the XG session information.
runIDs
The parameter contains the system-generated numbers that identify the runs.
To obtain a run ID, you use the SearchRuns method to search for the run.

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 106

CONFIDENTIAL

Return Values
If all the runs are deleted, then response returns Null.
If any runs were not deleted, then the response returns a list of the batch run IDs that identify the
runs that were not deleted.
Related Information
ClientContext Class on page 22
SearchRuns Method on page 108
DeleteRuns Code Example on page 228

runID

Result Management
The Results interface lets you manage the alerts that are stored in the XG database.
The Results interface lets you perform the following actions on alerts:
•
•
•
•

View an alert that contains specific information.
Delete an alert.
Query for alerts that contain specific information.
Set the record state for an alert.

Related Information
C# Code Examples on page 211

DeleteResultRecords Method
The DeleteResultRecords method deletes the specified alerts.
Syntax
List<long> DeleteResultRecords(ClientContext context, List<long> resultIDs)

Parameters
The method contains the following parameters:
context
The ClientContext class contains the XG client information and the XG session information.
resultIDs
The parameter contains the system-generated numbers that identify the alerts to be deleted.
The maximum number of records that can be deleted in one request is 1,000.
To obtain a result ID, you use the SearchResultRecords method to search for the alert. The ID is
also returned for the alert in a search response.

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 113

CONFIDENTIAL

Return Values
If all the alerts were deleted, then the response returns Null.
If any alerts were not deleted, then the response returns a list of result IDs that identifies the alerts
that were not deleted.
Related Information

SearchResultRecords Method
The SearchResultRecords method returns the alerts that meet the specified criteria in the result query.
Syntax
SearchRecordResults SearchResultRecords(ClientContext context, ResultsCriteria
criteria, long position, int numberToReturn)

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 114

CONFIDENTIAL

Parameters
The method contains the following parameters:
context
The ClientContext class contains the XG client information and the XG session information.
criteria
The ResultsCriteria class contains the criteria that alerts must meet to be returned in a result
query.
position
The parameter contains the position of the first record ID to be returned.
numberToReturn
The parameter contains the number of record IDs, up to 100, to be returned.
Return Values
The SearchRecordResults class contains the record IDs of the alerts that met the criteria in a result
query.
If no records were found or the specified position is beyond the end of the matching record, then the
response returns an empty list.
Related Information
ClientContext Class on page 22
ResultsCriteria Class on page 125

SetRecordState Method
The SetRecordState method changes a combination of case management options and workflow options
of an alert.
Syntax
bool SetRecordState(ClientContext context, long resultID, RecordState state)

Parameters
The method contains the following parameters:
context
The ClientContext class contains the XG client information and the XG session information.

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 115

CONFIDENTIAL

resultID
The parameter contains the system-generated number that identifies the alert.
To obtain a result ID, you use the SearchResultRecords method to search for the alert. The ID is
also returned for the alert in a search response.
state
The RecordState class contains a combination of case management options and workflow options
for the alert.
Return Values
If the method succeeds, then the response returns True.
If the method fails or generates an error, then the response returns an Error class.

Chapter 6

L is t M ai n tenance Interface
LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG (XG) web services provide a ListMaintenance interface that you can use
to manage accept lists and custom screening lists.
Accept lists use information that you added from previous XG searches to filter out list screening
matches in new searches that you have already processed. Your organization has likely already
determined that those matches were false positive or has determined that updates to the entity records
in the match need to be monitored.
For more information about how accept lists work, see the Accept Lists and White List technical
white paper that is available on the LexisNexis® Risk Solutions Customer Support Hub at https://
lnrs.my.site.com/CustomerSupportHub/s/article/1969.
Custom screening lists are used to flag countries or entities in list searches for purposes that are unique
to your organization.

List Management
The ListMaintenance interface lets you manage accept lists or custom screening lists.
The ListMaintenance interface lets you perform the following actions on the lists:
•
•
•
•
•

Add a list.
Delete a list.
Search for a list that contains specific information.
Update a list.
View a list.

XG 5 clients can also index a custom screening list.
Lists that are set to automatically index do not index when changes are made through XG
web services. Before changes are reflected in XG, the list must be manually indexed in the XG
application or using the IndexList method.
Related Information
IndexList Method on page 138
C# Code Examples on page 211

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 135

CONFIDENTIAL

AddList Method
The AddList method creates a new accept list or custom screening list.
Records must be added to a custom screening list before the list can be included in a search. The XG 5
custom screening lists must be indexed before they can be included in a search.
XG Enterprise shared lists that need to be available to other product client instances must be
created in the XG application.
Syntax
long AddList(ClientContext context, ListInfo list)

Parameters
The method contains the following parameters:
context
The ClientContext class contains the XG client information and the XG session information.
list
The ListInfo class contains the list information when you take action on a list.
Return Values
The response returns the system primary key that identifies the list.
If the method fails or generates an error, then the response returns an Error class.
Related Information
ClientContext Class on page 22
ListInfo Class on page 140
ServiceFault Class on page 204
AddList Code Example on page 219

DeleteList Method
The DeleteList method deletes the specified list.
You cannot delete the default accept list.
Before you delete a list, remove the list from the predefined searches in the XG application. You should
also remove the list from the alert decisions. You may want to export the list before you delete the list to
retain a copy for your audit records.
The changes that are made to a custom screening list are not available until the list is indexed.

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

listID

To obtain the list ID, you use the SearchLists method to search for the list.

If the method succeeds, then the response returns True.
If the method fails or generates an error, then the response returns an Error class.

AddRecords Method
The AddRecords method adds records that were not generated by a search to a specified custom
screening list.
This method cannot be used to add records to accept lists.
The changes that are made to a custom screening list are not available until the list is indexed.
Syntax
List<AddRecordResult> AddRecords(ClientContext context, long listID,
List<ListRecord> records)

Parameters
The method contains the following parameters:
context
The ClientContext class contains the XG client information and the XG session information.
listID
The parameter contains the system-generated primary key that identifies the list.
To obtain the list ID, you use the SearchLists method to search for the list.
records
The ListRecord class contains the record information when you add a record, update a record, or
view record information.
The request must contain all entity records or all country records. The type of record that is
required depends on the type of custom screening list that you want to add the records to.
Return Values
The AddRecordResult class contains the information about the record that was added to the list.

AddResultRecord Method
The AddResultRecord method adds a specified alert to an accept list or to an entity custom screening list.
You cannot add an alert to a country custom screening list.
When you add an alert to an accept list, XG automatically changes the record as follows:
• The alert status is set to FalsePositive.
• The alert assignment is set to Unassigned.
• The alert state is set to Closed.
The changes that are made to a custom screening list are not available until the list is indexed.
Syntax
long AddResultRecord(ClientContext context, long listID, ResultInfo result)

Parameters
The method contains the following parameters:
context
The ClientContext class contains the XG client information and the XG session information.
listID
The parameter contains the system-generated primary key that identifies the list.
To obtain the list ID, you use the SearchLists method to search for the list.
result
The ResultInfo class contains the alert information that XG used to create the list record.
Return Values
The response contains the system-generated primary key that identifies the list record.
Related Information
ClientContext Class on page 22
SearchLists Method on page 138

CONFIDENTIAL

DeleteRecords Method
The DeleteRecords method deletes specified records in a list. You may want to export the list before you
delete the records to retain a copy for your audit records.
The changes that are made to a custom screening list are not available until the list is indexed.
Syntax
List<long> DeleteRecords(ClientContext context, long listID, List<long> recordIDs)

Parameters
The method contains the following parameters:
context
The ClientContext class contains the XG client information and the XG session information.
listID
The parameter contains the system-generated primary key that identifies the list.
To obtain the list ID, you use the SearchLists method to search for the list.
recordIDs
A list of system-generated numbers that identify the records to be deleted.
The maximum number of records that can be deleted in one request is 100.
To obtain a record ID, you use the SearchListRecords method to search for the record.
Return Values
If all the records were successfully deleted, then the response returns Null.
If any of the selected records were not deleted, then the response returns a list of record IDs for the
records that were not deleted.
Related Information
ClientContext Class on page 22
SearchLists Method on page 138
SearchListRecords Method on page 146
DeleteRecords Code Example on page 213

SearchListRecords Method
The SearchListRecords method returns records in a specified list that meet the specified criteria.
Syntax
SearchRecordResults SearchListRecords(ClientContext context, long listID,
ListRecordCriteria criteria, long position, int numberToReturn)

Parameters
The method contains the following parameters:
context
The ClientContext class contains the XG client information and the XG session information.

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 146

CONFIDENTIAL

listID
The parameter contains the system-generated primary key that identifies the list.
To obtain the list ID, you use the SearchLists method to search for the list.
criteria
The ListRecord class contains the record information when you add a record, update a record, or
view record information.
position
The position, in the list, of the record ID of the first record to be returned.
numberToReturn
The number of record IDs, up to 100, to be returned.
Return Values
The SearchRecordResults class contains the record IDs of the alerts that met the criteria in a result
query.

Chapter 7

E FT Par se d Input C las ses
With the Search method in the Search interface, input EFT (electronic funds transfer) data, or payment
transaction data, is searched as a text string that is provided in the InputEFT class. LexisNexis®
Bridger Insight® XG (XG) web services return the input payment transaction data as structured
information when a potential list match is reported.

ParsedISO20022 Class
The ParsedISO20022 class contains the ISO 20022 input information. The class contains some SWIFT
(Society for Worldwide Interbank Financial Telecommunication) ISO 20022 information that is available
only for searches that use the SWIFT EFT input type.

about the new SWIFT ISO 20022 standard, see https://www.swift.com/standards/iso-20022.

LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG (XG) web services include entity information in a number of methods
that are available in the Search interface, the Results interface, or the List Maintenance interface.

Input Entity Classes
With the Search method in the Search interface, the input entity classes can be provided in the request
or returned in the response. XG can also return this information from result queries that are performed
in the Results interface.
Related Information
Search Input Classes on page 53
Record Information Classes on page 62
Result Management Classes on page 116

Date Class
The Date class contains date information.
When possible, you should use the parsed elements instead of the Unparsed element for optimal
results.
Class Elements
Name

Type

Description

Integer

date.

date.

Class Elements (Continued)
Name

Type

Description

Unparsed

String

This element contains the unstructured date value.
If your client instance is configured to use the ISO
(International Organization for Standardization) date
format in web services, then input dates are required
to be in a YYYY-MM-DD format. If your client instance
is configured to use U.S. or U.K. formats in web
services, then no format requirements exist for input
dates.

Year

Integer

This element contains the year value in a structured
date.

InputAccount Class
The InputAccount class contains the account information that helps identify the input entity.
An account number can be provided in the InputID class. The following account information can also be
provided in the InputID class: account type, member ID, and provider ID. If this information is provided in
both classes, then only the data in the InputAccount class is added to the record.

InputID Class
The InputID class contains the input ID information. The input ID may be included in either an
InputEntity element search, an InputText element search, or an InputBasicID element search.
The following account information can also be provided in the InputAccount class: account type,
member ID, and provider ID. If this information is provided in both classes, then only the data in the
InputAccount class is added to the record.

InputName Class
The InputName class contains the input name information. This class is required for Search requests that
use the InputEntity element to search structured information.
For individual entities, the First element and the Last element are required or the Full element is
required. For business entities or unknown entities, the Full element is required.
Records that contain the Full element can only be searched against screening lists.
All records within a request must contain the same elements.
Class Elements
Name

Type

Description

First

String

This element contains the first name.
You use this element only for individual entities.

Generation

This element contains the full name.

III.
You use this element only for individual entities.

This element contains the last name.
You use this element only for individual entities.

String

This element contains the maiden name.
You use this element only for individual entities.

String

This element contains the middle name.
You use this element only for individual entities.

String

This element contains the second surname.
You use this element only for individual entities.

Title

String

This element contains the title.
You use this element only for individual entities.

Entity Criteria Classes
The entity criteria classes can be provided in the result queries that are performed in the Results
interface or in the list record queries that are performed in the List Maintenance interface.
Related Information
Result Management Classes on page 116
List Record Management Classes on page 148

EntityCriteriaAdditionalInfo Class
The EntityCriteriaAdditionalInfo class contains the additional information that the record must meet to
be returned.
If only one of the Value1 or Value2 elements is provided, then the record information must meet
that value. For example, you set the Type to Citizenship and provide United States in the Value1
element. Only records that contain a Citizenship of United States are returned.
If both elements are provided, then the record information must meet a value within the provided
range. For example, you set the Type to DOB and provide 01/01/1955 in the Value1 element
and 01/01/1965 for the Value2 element. Only records that contain a DOB within the range of
01/01/1955-01/01/1965 are returned.
Class Elements
Name

Type

Description

Type

AdditionalInfoType

This element contains the additional information type.
This element is required.

Value1

String

Value2

String

This element contains additional information that is
contained in the record, or the start of the range that
includes the additional information.
This element contains additional information that is
contained in the record, or the end of the range that
includes the additional information.

Related Information
Possible Additional Information Types on page 198

Possible Type Values
A number of classes contain additional information or IDs for entities in the Search interface, the Results
interface, or the List Maintenance interface. These classes include a Type element that indicates the kind
of information the class provides.

Chapter 9

E r r or s
LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG (XG) web services can return service fault errors that prevented the
request from being completed and result errors that were returned from searches.

ResultError Class
The ResultError class returns any errors that were generated during a search.
Class Elements
Name

Type

Description

Code

Unsigned Integer

This element contains the error code.
Not all errors contain an error code.

Message

String

This element contains the error message.

Related Information
Error Messages on page 200
Error Codes on page 202

Error Messages
If an error occurs, then XG web services may return an error message.
These messages are specific to XG web services. Other messages that are related to XG may be
returned as well.

ServiceFault Class
The ServiceFault class returns any errors that were generated by the system or method.
Class Elements
Name

Type

Description

Message
Type

String
ServiceFaultType

This element contains the ServiceFault error message.
This element contains the ServiceFault type. Possible
values:
• AccessDenied
• Error
• FreeTrialLapsed
• InvalidCredentials
• MustChangePassword
• PasswordExpired
• UnsupportedVersion
• UserDisabled
• UserLocked
• WatchlistsExpired

Related Information
ServiceFault Error Messages on page 204

ServiceFault Error Messages
ServiceFault errors contain the following text: The following error occurred while processing
your request. Please contact your system administrator.
The errors also include the XG error message, a search message, or one of the messages in the following
table.

C # C od e Exa mpl es
LexisNexis® Risk Solutions provides C# code examples.

AddRecord Code Example
Code examples can help you understand how to use the methods in LexisNexis® Bridger Insight® XG (XG)
web services.
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
// Function: AddRecord
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
//Create a client.
XgServices.ListMaintenanceClient ListClient = new XgServices.ListMaintenanceClient();
//Set the endpoint for the client. It will have a different value for production and test.
ListClient.Endpoint.Address = new System.ServiceModel.EndpointAddress
("https://bridgerinsight.lexisnexis.com/LN.WebServices/12.0/xgservices.svc/ListMaintenance");
//Set up the context.
XgServices.ClientContext Context = new XgServices.ClientContext();
Context.ClientID = "ClientID";
Context.UserID = "UserID";
Context.Password = "Password";
//Choose the list. Look up via searchLists if necessary.
long ListID = 5;
//Create an array of records to add.
XgServices.ListRecord[] ListRecords = new XgServices.ListRecord[1];
//Create a record.
ListRecords[0] = new XgServices.ListRecord();
ListRecords[0].Entity = new XgServices.EntityInfo();
ListRecords[0].Entity.Name = new XgServices.EntityName();
ListRecords[0].Entity.Name.Full = "NewEntity FullName";
ListRecords[0].Entity.Name.Full = "NewEntity FullName";
ListRecords[0].Entity.EntityType = XgServices.ListEntityType.Individual;
XgServices.AddRecordResult[] Results = ListClient.AddRecords(Context,ListID,ListRecords);

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 211

CONFIDENTIAL

///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
// END Function: AddRecord
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

Related Information
AddRecords Method on page 143

// Function: AddResultRecord

XgServices.ListMaintenanceClient ListClient = new XgServices.ListMaintenanceClient();

("https://bridgerinsight.lexisnexis.com/LN.WebServices/12.0/xgservices.svc/ListMaintenance");

Context.UserID = "UserID";
Context.Password = "Password";
//Set the list to add the list to. Look up the list ID via searchLists if necessary.
long ListID = 1;
//Set the alert state information to change.
XgServices.ResultInfo result = new XgServices.ResultInfo();
result.NewAlertState = XgServices.AlertStateType.Closed;
result.NewStatus = "False Positive";
result.Note = "Adding To Accept List Via Web Services";
result.ResultID = 688;
long listRecord = ListClient.AddResultRecord(Context, ListID, result);

("https://bridgerinsight.lexisnexis.com/LN.WebServices/12.0/xgservices.svc/ListMaintenance");

Context.Password = "Password";
//Set the list. Look up the list ID via searchLists if necessary.
long ListID = 1;
//Set the record to update.
XgServices.ArrayOfLong listRecords = new XgServices.ArrayOfLong();
listRecords.Add(31478);

XgServices.ListRecord[] ReturnedRecords = ListClient.GetRecords(Context, ListID, listRecords);

SearchListRecords Code Example
Code examples can help you understand how to use the methods in XG web services.
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
// Function: SearchListRecords
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
//Create a client.
XgServices.ListMaintenanceClient ListClient = new XgServices.ListMaintenanceClient();
//Set the endpoint for the client. It will have a different value for production and test.
ListClient.Endpoint.Address = new System.ServiceModel.EndpointAddress
("https://bridgerinsight.lexisnexis.com/LN.WebServices/12.0/xgservices.svc/ListMaintenance");
//Set up the context.
XgServices.ClientContext Context = new XgServices.ClientContext();
Context.ClientID = "ClientID";
Context.UserID = "UserID";
Context.Password = "Password";
//Set the list. Look up the list ID via searchLists if necessary.
long ListID = 1;
//Set the record criteria.
XgServices.ListRecordCriteria Criteria = new XgServices.ListRecordCriteria();
Criteria.DateListedStart = new XgServices.Date();
Criteria.DateListedStart.Day = 1;
Criteria.DateListedStart.Month = 1;
Criteria.DateListedStart.Year = 2000;
//Requires and end.
Criteria.DateListedEnd = new XgServices.Date();
Criteria.DateListedEnd.Day = 1;
Criteria.DateListedEnd.Month = 1;
Criteria.DateListedEnd.Year = 2014;
int StartPosition = 0;
int ReturnCount = 100; //Maximum of 100
XgServices.SearchRecordResults ReturnedRecords = ListClient.SearchListRecords(Context,
ListID, Criteria, StartPosition, ReturnCount);
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
// END Function: SearchListRecords
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

UpdateList Code Example
Code examples can help you understand how to use the methods in XG web services.
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
// Function: UpdateList
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
//Create a client.
XgServices.ListMaintenanceClient ListClient = new XgServices.ListMaintenanceClient();
//Set the endpoint for the client. It will have a different value for production and test.
ListClient.Endpoint.Address = new System.ServiceModel.EndpointAddress
("https://bridgerinsight.lexisnexis.com/LN.WebServices/12.0/xgservices.svc/ListMaintenance");
//Set up the context.
XgServices.ClientContext Context = new XgServices.ClientContext();
Context.ClientID = "ClientID";
Context.UserID = "UserID";
Context.Password = "Password";
//Set the list to get for an update.
long listID = 1;
XgServices.ListInfo ListReturn = ListClient.GetList(Context, listID);
//Change list information.
//Note - Any list information elements that are not included will be deleted from the
//
existing list settings
ListReturn.Name = "List Display Name";
ListReturn.Type = "Accept or Custom";
ListReturn.Description = "We are updating the description via web services";
ListReturn.UniqueID = "DB109D85-F167-4E22-918C-760B39AB0CB8";
//Write it back to XG.
bool Success = ListClient.UpdateList(Context, ListReturn);
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
// END Function: UpdateList

Search Code Example
Code examples can help you understand how to use the methods in XG web services.
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
// Function: Search
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
//Create a client.
XgServices.SearchClient SearchClient = new XgServices.SearchClient();
//Set the endpoint for the client. It will have a different value for production and test.
SearchClient.Endpoint.Address = new System.ServiceModel.EndpointAddress
("https://bridgerinsight.lexisnexis.com/LN.WebServices/12.0/xgservices.svc/Search");
//Set up context, configuration, and input information.
XgServices.SearchInput Input = new XgServices.SearchInput();
//Set up the context.
XgServices.ClientContext Context = new XgServices.ClientContext();
Context.ClientID = "ClientID";
Context.UserID = "UserID";
Context.Password = "Password";
Context.ClientReference = "GUID here Please";
Context.GLB = 5;
Context.DPPA = XgServices.DPPAChoiceType.Choice3;
//Set up the configuration.
XgServices.SearchConfiguration Config = new XgServices.SearchConfiguration();
Config.PredefinedSearchName = "List Screening";
//Set the alert assignment.
Config.AssignResultTo = new XgServices.AssignmentInfo();
Config.AssignResultTo.RolesOrUsers = new XgServices.ArrayOfString();
Config.AssignResultTo.Type = XgServices.AssignmentType.Role;
Config.AssignResultTo.RolesOrUsers.Add("Administrator");
Config.WriteResultsToDatabase = true;
//Set up the input information.
Input.Records = new XgServices.InputRecord[1];
Input.Records[0] = new XgServices.InputRecord();
Input.Records[0].Entity = new XgServices.InputEntity();
Input.Records[0].Entity.EntityType = XgServices.InputEntityType.Individual;
Input.Records[0].Entity.Name = new XgServices.InputName();
Input.Records[0].Entity.Name.First = "Charles";
Input.Records[0].Entity.Name.Last = "Taylor";
//Provide the input information.

BIS393-EN_US — 28 December 2023

SOAP API 12.0 for XG 5 Web Services Page 224

CONFIDENTIAL

Input.Records[0].Entity.IDs = new XgServices.InputID[1];
Input.Records[0].Entity.IDs[0] = new XgServices.InputID();
Input.Records[0].Entity.IDs[0].Type = XgServices.IDType.SSN;
Input.Records[0].Entity.IDs[0].Number = "1234";
Input.Records[0].Entity.AdditionalInfo = new XgServices.InputAdditionalInfo[1];
Input.Records[0].Entity.AdditionalInfo[0] = new XgServices.InputAdditionalInfo();
Input.Records[0].Entity.AdditionalInfo[0].Type = XgServices.AdditionalInfoType.Incident;
Input.Records[0].Entity.AdditionalInfo[0].Value = "Rejected";
//Call the search.
XgServices.SearchResults Result = SearchClient.Search(Context, Config, Input);
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
// END Function: Search
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

Related Information
Search Method on page 28

SearchRuns Code Example
Code examples can help you understand how to use the methods in XG web services.
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
// Function: SearchRuns
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
//Create a client.
XgServices.ResultsClient ResultsClient = new XgServices.ResultsClient();
//Set the endpoint for the client. It will have a different value for production and test.
ResultsClient.Endpoint.Address = new System.ServiceModel.EndpointAddress
("https://bridgerinsight.lexisnexis.com/LN.WebServices/12.0/xgservices.svc/Results");
//Set up the context.
XgServices.ClientContext Context = new XgServices.ClientContext();
Context.ClientID = "ClientID";
Context.UserID = "UserID";
Context.Password = "Password";
//Set run criteria.
XgServices.RunsCriteria Criteria = new XgServices.RunsCriteria();
//NOTE: Limit your criteria carefully. A large amount of data is returned for each run.
Criteria.DateStart = new XgServices.Date();
Criteria.DateStart.Day = 1;
Criteria.DateStart.Month = 1;
Criteria.DateStart.Year = 2013;
Criteria.SubmitType = XgServices.RunsCritieraSubmitType.Batch;
XgServices.RunInfo[] Response = ResultsClient.SearchRuns(Context, Criteria);
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
// END Function: SearchRuns

Criteria.DateStart.Month = 6;
